This is an image system with 2a and 2b very close to the critical curve, where the two images almost meet to form a long vertical line. Image 2c is rather isolated and appears almost unresolved. As seen in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf14\">14</a>, de-lens and re-lens 2a and 2b successfully reproduced the long vertical line very similar to observation. However, re-lens 2c produced a curved line in the region of 2a and 2b.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf14\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf14\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf14_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 14.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 14.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf14_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 14.</strong>\u00a0Here we provide our own model reconstruction of image 2a and 2b from system 2, using the pixels of image 2a to generate the other image for comparison with the observed images. This reconstruction is made by solving for the lens equation, and then de-lensing followed by re-lensing of the observed flux in each pixel. Notice that for image 2b, our mass model is even able to reproduce the small left curve of the observed image. The white curve shows the critical curve at the redshift of system 2.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf14\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf14\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa4efcf14\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf14\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>System 3. This system lies very close to MACS0647-JD, the high-redshift candidate. There are two identified images, quite close to each other. Our mass model predicts a third image at the top left part of the field of view, as labeled in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf1\">1</a>. After searching through the data, we could not find the image without ambiguity. Our predicted brightness for this image is comparable with the noise in the F475 band where it should be strongest (AB magnitude ~29.4), which is consistent with its lack of detection. We do not include any third image candidate into our constraints. As the system is so close to our <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a011 candidate, it serves as a good indicator of whether <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a011 is a reliable redshift of system 6 using the \"geometric\" method, as we demonstrated above.</p><p>System 4. This system is a triply lensed galaxy. One of the multiply lensed images, 4a, lies closely to a cluster member galaxy. Our model successfully delens and re-lens other images to the position of 4a. Further investigation on the morphology of that image can be done to constrain the mass model of the cluster member galaxy.</p><p>System 5. A very faint doubly lensed image system, which is the second-highest redshift galaxy identified in the lensing field.</p><p>System 6. The second-highest redshift galaxy ever observed, and the highest redshift lensed galaxy identified. Using our best mass model, we predict a geometric redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a010.8, coincide with the photometric redshift derived by Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>).</p><p>System 7. This is a triply lensed spiral galaxy lies near to system 1. The images are well resolved, and slightly fainter than system 1. The source has the same photometric redshift as system 1 but with slight offset in position.</p><p>System 8. This doubly lensed system exhibits major lensing effect from a nearby cluster member galaxy. As shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf12\">12</a>, our model is able to reproduce the relensed centroids of both multiple images. The re-lens result predicts a third image 8c at a position near image 1b and 7b, with predicted brightness similar to that of 8a. With careful inspection at the predicted region, we could not find the image without ambiguity. As 8a and 8b lie closely to the critical curve, the morphology is highly distorted. For this reason, it is more challenging to identify the counter-image.</p><p>System 9. This system is among the faintest galaxies in the lensing field. With hugely separated positions of multiply lensed images, it provides useful constraints to the mass model.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa4efcs7\" name=\"apjaa4efcs7\">7.\u00a0LENS MODEL PREDICTION USING RELATIVE BRIGHTNESSES.</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Having demonstrated above the reliability of the high-redshift option for MACS0647-JD, we now make use of its redshift to evaluate the predictive power of our lensing model by looking at the relative fluxes of all the multiply lensed systems. The evaluation was first made in Broadhurst et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib5\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib5\">2005</a>) for the case of A1689 and recently for the first HFF cluster A2744 by Lam et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib37\">2014</a>) using our free-form WSLAP+ code. Note that the information contained in the relative brightness of individual sets of lensed images is not used when constructing the lens model.</p><p>In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf15\">15</a> we plot the model-predicted relative magnitudes against the observed magnitudes for the images that constrained the reconstructed lens model. The magnitudes are predicted by magnifying or de-magnifying the observed magnitudes of the first and second images in each system, as typically there are three images per system with usually one case where the photometry is poor due to overlap with a member galaxy. Reassuringly, we find a clear linear relation between the predicted and observed magnitudes, indicating the high level of predictive power of our model. There are a few outliers attributable to the proximity to the critical curve to the ended image so that the correction is relatively large, but in general the overall scatter is small and the trend shows no systematic deviation from linearity. The scatter in this relation, however, significantly exceeds the photometric uncertainty. We are currently examining how we can incorporate the relative brightness of the lens images as additional constraints when modeling the cluster lens. We present these results in (Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf16\">16</a>), where the observational parameters are compared to the model dependent parameters and we provide our predictions for the intrinsic brightness of MACS0647-JD in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa4efct4\">4</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf15\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf15\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf15_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 15.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 15.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf15_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 15.</strong>\u00a0Relative magnitudes predicted by our model plotted against observed magnitudes of multiple images. The predicted magnitudes are calculated by magnifying the observed magnitudes of the first images in each system by our lens model.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf15\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf15\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa4efcf15\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf15\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf16\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf16\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf16_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 16.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; valign=\"top\">\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"left\"><em>M</em><sub><em>UV</em></sub></td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u221219.6</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u221219.41</td>\n<td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\" align=\"center\">\u221219.32</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<p><strong>Note.</strong> The F160W flux here was adapted from Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>) Fluxes in nanoJanskys (nJy) may be converted to AB magnitudes via <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcieqn21.gif\" alt=\"${m}_{{AB}}\\sim 26\\mbox{--}2.5\\mathrm{log}({F}_{\\nu }/(145{nJy}))$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">{m}_{{AB}}\\sim 26\\mbox{--}2.5\\mathrm{log}({F}_{\\nu }/(145{nJy}))</script></span></span>.</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/suppdata/apjaa4efct4_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/835/1/44\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/suppdata/apjaa4efct4_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa4efcs8\" name=\"apjaa4efcs8\">8.\u00a0GEOMETRIC REDSHIFT CONSISTENCY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Here we look in turn at each system of multiple images and ask how well the geometric redshift that we derive for it agrees with the measured photometric redshift. This can be done by constructing a set of lens models where we leave out each system in turn and then use that corresponding model to estimate the geometric redshift of that system that was left out of its construction. The result of this procedure is shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf17\">17</a>, where we plot the predicted geometric redshift of all systems against their photometric redshifts as measured by Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>). To compute their geometric redshifts, we reconstructed nine different mass models, each with one of the systems not included in the initial constraint. We then compute the average and standard deviation of the predicted geometric redshifts out of all nine models. As can be seen from the figure, the data points lie close to the correspondence line, with errors within 1<em>\u03c3</em>. The consistency between the photometric and geometric redshifts is striking and indicates that there is no obvious outlier with an unreliable photometric redshift.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf17\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf17\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf17_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 17.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 17.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf17_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 17.</strong>\u00a0Here we show the predicted geometric redshifts and the photometric redshifts of all the multiply lensed systems . Values and errors of photometric redshifts obtained from Coe et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>) are shown in blue points. Three systems identified by Zitrin et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>) are shown as pink points, with each point representing an individual counter-image. The faintest pink point shows the result for image 10.2, which has a relatively large error on its photometric redshift measurement. The green line is the one to one correspondence line, while the dash line shows the redshift of the lensing cluster. The values and errors in geometric redshift is calculated by averaging nine reconstructed mass models for testing each lensed system, where with the system in question is not included in the construction of the set of mass model with which its geometric redshift is evaluated. The red dash line shows the redshift of the lensing cluster MACS0647. From the graph, the image with photometric redshift <em>z</em> = 0.41 cannot be lensed as it is in front of the lensing cluster. In such case geometric redshift is useful to estimate the redshift of a galaxy.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf17\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf17\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa4efcf17\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf17\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa4efcs9\" name=\"apjaa4efcs9\">9.\u00a0OTHER CANDIDATE LENSED SYSTEMS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Apart from nine secured lensed systems as identified in Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>), three more candidate lensed systems were identified by Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>). The details of these candidate systems are shown in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa4efct5\">5</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"apjaa4efct5\"    <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/suppdata/apjaa4efct5_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-4357/835/1/44\" image</a></span></p></div><p>System 10. This system consists of two multiply lensed images. A slight difference is observed for the most likely photometric redshift of counter-images. The redshift error of image 10.2 is quite large related to ambiguity in the SED fitting. Our geometric redshift agrees well with the photometric redshift of image 10.1.</p><p>System 11. There is a huge disagreement in photometric redshifts between the counter-images. The geometric redshift predicted for this system lies at <em>z</em> = 1.95, corresponding approximately to the average of the photometric redshift measured.</p><p>System 12. Although photometric redshfit is not available for 12.1, there is a good agreement between 12.2 and 12.3. The geometric redshift predicted agrees very well with the photometric redshift.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa4efcs10\" name=\"apjaa4efcs10\">10.\u00a0DISCUSSION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Previous lens modeling has not provided a definitive geometric redshift for system 6, or indeed for any other system lensed by this cluster. In Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>), the larger critical curve at <em>z</em> = 11 does pass centrally between images 6a and 6b like in our model and the critical curves are fairly similar (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf18\">18</a>) so that we can imagine the form of parametric modeling might lead to consistency in this respect. In Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>) an attempt was made to find good solutions in the context of the \"light traces mass\" approach, which has a degree of flexibility and a minimum of free parameters. Two solutions were presented by Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>) as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf18\">18</a> where the more elliptical of the two cases favors high-redshift. Our free-form model has the desirable approach of providing a definitive geometric redshift for all the lensed galaxies here that are not dependent on profile parameters, but to a free-form mass distribution that is very general. Note also that, as discussed in Sections <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs6-2\">6.2</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs8\">8</a>, the geometric redshifts we determine for all systems in this work are in good agreement with their independently determined photometric redshifts. Furthermore, the predictive power in getting the relative magnifications of lensed images was demonstrated in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs7\">7</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf18\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf18\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf18_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 18.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 18.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf18_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 18.</strong>\u00a0Here we compare our critical curves for our best-fit free-form model (top) with those from Coe et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>) (middle) that uses the parametric Lenstool model, and also a pair of solutions taken from Zitrin et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>) for which two good solutions were found (bottom). Note that in all cases the size of the critical curves increases with redshift and the corresponding redshifts are marked. Note that the more elliptical model of Zitrin et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>) agrees well with the shape of our critical curves and those of Coe et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf18\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf18\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa4efcf18\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf18\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>In addition to the high-redshift galaxy that we have analyzed here finding a high geometric redshift of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcieqn22.gif\" alt=\"$z\\simeq {10.8}_{-0.4}^{+0.3}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\simeq {10.8}_{-0.4}^{+0.3}</script></span></span> for MACS0647-JD, the same free-form method has been successful in determining the geometric redshifts of Hubble frontier field galaxies, including a triply lensed galaxy with a photometric redshift of <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a09.6 behind A2744 and a confirming geometric redshift (Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib70\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib70\">2014</a>) from our free-form method.</p><p>MACS0647-JD is the highest redshift galaxy so far detected from lensing despite two magnitudes of magnification and the great depth of this imaging, no lensed galaxy is yet discovered beyond the most distant galaxies already known for several years (Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib64\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib64\">2012</a>; Coe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib8\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib8\">2015</a>; Oesch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib46\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib46\">2013</a>; Zitrin et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib70\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib70\">2014</a>; Ishigaki et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib33\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib33\">2015</a>). This difficulty is not due to the filter choice, which in principle can access Lyman-break galaxies out to <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a012. As the HFF program progresses to completion we may anticipate a clear, field-averaged constraint on the number density of galaxies lying above <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a09.0. A significant absence of such galaxies is not predicted for the LCDM model, where several galaxies are expected per HFF cluster in the range 9\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a010 on the basis of the standard LCDM model, by extrapolating the luminosity function (e.g., Coe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib8\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib8\">2015</a>; Schive et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib58\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib58\">2016</a>).</p><p>The most recent work by Oesch et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib48\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib48\">2015</a>) and Bouwens (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib3\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib3\">2016</a>) in relation to the deep-field surveys has indicated a surprisingly complex picture that confirms the rapid decline in the integrated star formation above <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a08, exceeding the extrapolated rate from the well defined 3\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a08 range together with several new claims of relatively relatively bright field galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a010 including one with <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a011 .1 supported by <em>HST</em> grism observations. A clear dearth of lower luminosity galaxies may also indicate in the latest (Bouwens et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib2\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib2\">2015</a>) work at 8\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a010 and this is in contrast to the rising luminosity functions reported by Dunlop et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib19\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib19\">2016</a>), for the HFF and other deep fields, though this rests on the reliability of very faint sources near the flux limit. It is interesting to speculate that the enhanced gas cooling is indicated in the case of wave-DM (Schive et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib57\">2014</a>) due to the massive dense solitonic core that form first in this context, quite unlike that of LCDM where the smallest galaxies form first with very inefficient star formation expected as winds readily remove hot gas from these small first halos (Franx et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib24\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib24\">1997</a>; Frye &amp; Broadhurst <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib25\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib25\">1998</a>; Pettini et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib49\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib49\">1998</a>; Frye et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib26\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib26\">2000</a>; Scannapieco &amp; Broadhurst <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib56\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib56\">2000</a>; Ferrara &amp; Loeb <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib22\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib22\">2013</a>). In this axion-like interpretation of CDM structure forms in the same way as standard heavy particle CDM on large scales (Schive et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib57\">2014</a>), but is suppressed below an inherent Jeans scale in the dark matter (Sikivie &amp; Yang <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib62\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib62\">2009</a>) so that the onset of galaxy formation is delayed with respect to CDM (Bozek et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib4\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib4\">2014</a>; Schive et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib57\">2014</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib58\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib58\">2016</a>). Whereas the onset of AGN activity may be relatively earlier than LCDM, because within <em>\u03c8</em>DM halos, a dense \"solitonic\" standing-wave core forms initially, of up to 10<sup>10</sup> <em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>, capable of focusing gas, seeding and feeding early super massive black holes (Schive et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib57\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib57\">2014</a>).</p><p>In addition, expectations regarding galaxy formation are also in flux because of the latest downward revision in the redshift estimate for reionization at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a08 from <em>Planck </em>polarization measurements of the optical depth of electron scattering of the CMB (Planck Collaboration et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib51\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib51\">2016</a>). Empirically, this low redshift squares with the contested claim of an accelerated decline in the galaxy luminosity density at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a08 (Oesch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib46\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib46\">2013</a>; Bouwens et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib2\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib2\">2015</a>; McClure et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib41\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib41\">2016</a>). These deepest observations with the <em>HST </em>and <em>Planck </em>satellites may together be consistent in indicating a later and more sudden onset of galaxy formation than widely anticipated. Empirically, it appears that consistency is seen between the downwardly revised \"instantaneous redshift\" of reionization, <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a08, when most of the cosmologically distributed hydrogen had become reionized (Planck Collaboration et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib51\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib51\">2016</a>) with the tentative claim of an accelerated decline in the integrated star formation rate at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a08 (Oesch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib45\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib45\">2010</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib46\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib46\">2013</a>) and supported by a absence of any galaxy detected beyond <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />11.0 (Oesch et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib47\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib47\">2016</a>), despite increasingly deep Hubble Frontier Field imaging (Zheng et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib64\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib64\">2012</a>; Lam et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib37\">2014</a>; Diego et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib13\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib13\">2015b</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib15\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib15\">2015c</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib12\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib12\">2016a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib14\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib14\">2016b</a>). Late reionization is also supported by a marked decline above <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a07 in the incidence of Ly<em>\u03b1</em> emission from high-redshift galaxy spectroscopy, which can be reproduced by photoionizaton models with a much higher neutral fraction than anticipated (Choudhury et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib7\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib7\">2015</a>; Mesinger et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib43\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib43\">2015</a>), indicating later galaxy and QSO formation (Madau &amp; Haardt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib40\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib40\">2015</a>).</p><p>At face value all these observations now seem to be at odds with LCDM for which no preferred redshift of galaxy formation is anticipated as the growth of structure is scale free for collisionless, cold dark matter, so that a smooth decline in galaxy numbers is widely anticipated to beyond <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a020 with the first stars predicted formed at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a050 (Naoz et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib44\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib44\">2006</a>). For the same reason, the low optical depth emerging from <em>Planck</em> satellite CMB work also seems in tension with CDM. Earlier higher estimates of <em>\u03c4</em> were rather too large to be comfortably provided by galaxy photoionization alone within the context of LCDM with \"reasonable\" photoioization parameters, including the unknown UV-escape fraction and the hardness of ionising radiation spectrum (Robertson &amp; Ellis <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib53\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib53\">2012</a>; Robertson et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib54\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib54\">2014</a>). However, a large variation in forest transparency between the highest redshift QSO sightlines (Becker et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib1\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib1\">2015</a>) may point to relatively few UV sources and hence to AGN rather than star formation as the dominant source of photoionization (Madau &amp; Haardt <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib40\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib40\">2015</a>), with the necessary ionization may be provided by low luminosity AGNs forming a flatter redshift evolution for low luminosity QSOs in the 4\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a06 range (Glikman et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib28\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib28\">2011</a>; Giallongo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib27\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib27\">2015</a>) as pointed out by Madau &amp; Haardt (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib40\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib40\">2015</a>). In this case one may either conclude that the escape fraction from early galaxies is negligible, or that such galaxies are not formed and this possible absence is now supported by the lack of low-luminosity galaxies at <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a08, with important implications for the the nature of dark matter, as described above.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa4efcs11\" name=\"apjaa4efcs11\">11.\u00a0SUMMARY, CONCLUSIONS AND FUTURE WORK</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We have focused here on the geometric constraint that lensing can provide for the distance of the highest redshift galaxy claimed in deep lensing work. We show quite generally with our free-form lensing model that its geometric redshift must lie well above the lower redshift neighboring system at <em>z</em>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/sime.gif\" alt=\"sime\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a03.0 (system 3). Spectral confirmation has proven infeasible to date, but alternative solutions such as <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a02.5 dusty galaxies have been disfavored with high confidence (Coe et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>). Furthermore, we find that our free-form lens model based on all nine sets of multiple images clearly prefers a high redshift for MACS0647-JD, on grounds both of its position and the relative image brightnesses. Our work clearly supports the high-redshift interpretation, with an independently determined geometric redshift that we have presented here of <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcieqn23.gif\" alt=\"$z\\simeq {10.8}_{-0.4}^{+0.3}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">z\\simeq {10.8}_{-0.4}^{+0.3}</script></span></span>. We also obtain an intrinsic luminosity of <em>M</em><sub>UV</sub> = \u221219.4 (corresponds to <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcieqn24.gif\" alt=\"$L/{L}_{z=3}^{* }\\,=\\,0.22$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">L/{L}_{z=3}^{* }\\,=\\,0.22</script></span></span>) that is close to that of Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>) but without associated model dependance. The calculated luminosity is a factor of a few lower compared with the objects mentioned in Holwerda et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib31\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib31\">2015</a>). Our work also supports two of the three new multiply lensed candidates tentatively identified by Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>), which we find show agreement between their geometric and photometric redshifts.</p><p>We have uncovered a satisfyingly tight agreement between our photometric redshifts and the \"geometric redshift\" that we derive for each multiply lensed system, as described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs8\">8</a> and shown in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apjaa4efct1\">1</a>. This good agreement indicates a high degree of self-consistency in the model, going well beyond the usual scatter in this type of figure such as in Broadhurst et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib5\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib5\">2005</a>) and Halkola et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib30\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib30\">2006</a>) for A1689, and explored also in a more model-dependent way by Limousin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib38\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib38\">2007</a>) for the NFW profile. Hence, the free-form model-independence of our method can in principle permit a joint constraint on the mass distribution and cosmology. The feasibility of this has been examined with simulations by Lubini et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib39\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib39\">2014</a>), and now seems warranted by our improved observational precision achieved here. We have also examined the self-consistency of the model by comparing the predicted and observed brightnesses of the lensed images as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf15\">15</a>. In principle we could also include this magnification related information when constraining the model, which will be done in future analysis.</p><p>This is the second such attempt to use the brightness data in a model-independent way, like the earlier work of Lam et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib37\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib37\">2014</a>), which utilized the same WSLAP+ code. We find a tight linear relation between the predicted relative magnitudes and the relative observed fluxes, demonstrating the predictive power of our lens model. This has not generally been found using parameterized model where the form of the radial profile of the cluster is limited to a narrow family of models (Caminha et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib6\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib6\">2016</a>) and further underscores the utility of our free-form approach in the case where the abundance of deep data justifies this method, over that of parameterized models. Parameterized models can only be partially appropriate at best for cluster mass distributions, particularly in the case of merging clusters where the complexities of tidal effects during encounters means the general mass distribution cannot be expected to adhere to a sum of idealized elliptical, power-law mass halos usually adopted. The improvements we have found here in using relative fluxes and local galaxy separations to constrain geometric distances motivates further exploration of the best means of combining the independent positional and flux data, for breaking the degeneracies allowed by positional data alone (Schneider &amp; Sluse <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib60\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib60\">2014</a>) with the goal of examining the cosmological-distance\u2013redshift relation in the unexplored range <em>z</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a02, beyond the supernovae Type Ia work, with our model-independent-lensing tools.</p></div> <div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The work is based on observations made with the NASA/ESA <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> and operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy, Inc. under NASA contract NAS 5-26555. T.J.B. gratefully acknowledges the Visiting Research Professor Scheme at the University of Hong Kong. J.M.D. acknowledges support of the consolider project AYA2015-64508-P (MINECO/FEDER, UE), CAD2010-00064 and AYA2012-39475-C02-01 funded by the Ministerio de Economia y Competitividad, and support from the Department of Physics at The University of Hong Kong for a visit to work on this project. J.L. acknowledges support from the University of Hong Kong via a Seed Funding Program for Basic Research through grant 201411159166 at the start of this project, thus enabling follow-up support from the Research Grants Council of Hong Kong through grant 17319316.</p></div><h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apjaa4efcapp1\" name=\"apjaa4efcapp1\">APPENDIX: MASS MAP UNCERTAINTIES</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Although the mass model we reconstruct shows a very high level of self-consistency and predicts well the relative brightnesses of lensed images, there is no strictly unique solution because the finite number of data points used effectively limits the spatial resolution of the reconstructed mass map. The grid construction is very general and hence inherently constrained in its freedom by the finite number of Gaussian pixels adopted. Here we investigate the accuracy of the mass map and its sensitivity to initial guesses for finding the best fit due to the inherent assumptions adopted when reconstructing the mass model.</p><h3 id=\"apjaa4efcapp1-1\" name=\"apjaa4efcapp1-1\">A.1.\u00a0Varying the Model Grid</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The reconstructed mass model will depend at some level on the number of Gaussian grids that we chose for the minimization. For our mass models derived above we found that 32\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a032 = 1024 grid points was a suitable choice in which self-consistent lens models can be generated. Now we investigate other choices, by construction the mass model with a relatively wide range of resolution: 23\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a023 = 529 to 38\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a038 = 1444 and measuring the standard deviation in the recovered mass over the surface of the mass map, as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf19\">19</a>. Here we can see the central region is generally well constrained by the multiply lensed region, the variation is generally very small with ~5% differences. However, the variation is noticeably larger in the outer region where the model cannot be as well constrained by the lack of distant counter-images well beyond the Einstein radius where the uncertainties rise to \u00a020%.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf19\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf19\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf19_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 19.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 19.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf19_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 19.</strong>\u00a0Background shows the ratio of the standard deviation map of our 16 mass models about the averaged mass map. These models differ by spanning a range of 3 in grid resolution. Mass contours of the mean mass model are overlaid on the mass variance map and the positions of multiply lensed images are overlaid on the map. Significant differences are only found outside the area covered by data.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf19\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf19\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa4efcf19\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf19\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjaa4efcapp1-2\" name=\"apjaa4efcapp1-2\">A.2.\u00a0Initial Assumptions Sensitivity</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>As described in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs4\">4</a>, the mass model was determined by solving a system of linear equation (Equation (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaa4efceqn3\">3</a>)). The unknowns are solved by minimizing a quadratic function that estimates the solution of Equations (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#apjaa4efceqn3\">3</a>). The minimization procedure was carried out in a series of orthogonal conjugate directions with an initial guess for the solution. The initial guess include the source positions and the mass included in each grid cell. The algorithm stops at a certain value which is determined to be a local minimum around the initial guess. For a highly degenerate case like this we could reach to different local minimum points starting with different initial assumed values. We construct 15 different mass models by varying the initial assumption values with the range between 0.5 and 1.5 times the original value, with the uncertainties shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf20\">20</a>.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf20\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf20\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf20_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 20.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 20.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf20_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 20.</strong>\u00a0Same as Figure <a href=\"#apjaa4efcf19\">19</a> but here shows the variability in initial guess.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf20\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf20\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa4efcf20\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf20\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjaa4efcapp1-3\" name=\"apjaa4efcapp1-3\">A.3.\u00a0Contribution of Photometric Redshift Uncertainty to Mass Map Variance</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We also include the photometric redshift uncertainty in our mass model, as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf21\">21</a>. Assuming a Gaussian probability distribution centering at the photometric redshift with FWHM of the uncertainty predicted by Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>). We reconstructed 15 mass models with the input redshifts of every source, drawn from a Gaussian distrubtion.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf21\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf21\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf21_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 21.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 21.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf21_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 21.</strong>\u00a0Same as Figure <a href=\"#apjaa4efcf19\">19</a> but here shows the variability in photometric redshift. Very little uncertainty in the mass map is produced by randomly varying the photometric redshifts within their respective estimated redshift uncertainties.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf21\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf21\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apjaa4efcf21\" href=\"/0004-637X/835/1/44/downloadHRFigure/figure/apjaa4efcf21\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div><h3 id=\"apjaa4efcapp1-4\" name=\"apjaa4efcapp1-4\">A.4.\u00a0Total Variance</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>As shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf22\">22</a>, we conclude that in the center there is evidence that the dominant source of variance in the mass map comes from the choice of starting position for the minimization, which for our purposes constitutes only a small uncertainty, which is noticeble within the central <em>r</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a05'' region, at a level of 15%. For most of the map only 5% variance is attributable to the central region, lying within the boundary of the multiply lensed images.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apjaa4efcf22\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apjaa4efcf22\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf22_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 22.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 22.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/835/1/44/Full/apjaa4efcf22_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 22.</strong>\u00a0Same as Figure <a href=\"#apjaa4efcf19\">19</a> but here shows the variability in all three effects. The dominant effect comes from the choice of starting position for the minimization, which for our purposes constitutes only a small uncertainty, that is noticeble near the center of mass at a level of 15%. For most of the map only 5% variance is attributable to all the above sources of noise for the region of interest, lying within the boundary of the multiply lensed image distribution.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apjaa4efcf22\" image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div></div></div><!-- End article full text -->\n<!-- Start Footnotes -->\n\t<h2 id=\"footnotes\">Footnotes</h2>\n\t\t<div In Coe et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib10\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib10\">2013</a>), the larger critical curve at <em>z</em> = 11 does pass centrally between images 6a and 6b like in our model and the critical curves are fairly similar (see Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf18\">18</a>) so that we can imagine the form of parametric modeling might lead to consistency in this respect. In Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>) an attempt was made to find good solutions in the context of the \"light traces mass\" approach, which has a degree of flexibility and a minimum of free parameters. Two solutions were presented by Zitrin et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apjaa4efcbib68\" id=\"fnref-apjaa4efcbib68\">2015a</a>) as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apjaa4efcf18\">18</a> where the more elliptical of the two cases favors high-redshift. Our free-form model has the desirable approach of providing a definitive geometric redshift for all the lensed galaxies here that are not dependent on profile parameters, but to a free-form mass distribution that is very general. Note also that, as discussed in Sections <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs6-2\">6.2</a> and <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs8\">8</a>, the geometric redshifts we determine for all systems in this work are in good agreement with their independently determined photometric redshifts. Furthermore, the predictive power in getting the relative magnifications of lensed images was demonstrated in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apjaa4efcs7\">7</a>."}, "Pandas format": {"Table 2": {"Status": "Complete", "Action": "Processed via pandas", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Skip cause table not important": "", "Message on table quality": "Source image info"}}}, "Table 3": {"Status": "Complete", "Action": "Processed via pandas", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Skip cause table not important": ""}}}, "Table 4": {"Status": "Complete", "Action": "Processed via pandas", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Skip cause table not important": ""}}}, "Table 5": {"Status": "Complete", "Action": "Processed via pandas", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Skip cause table not important": ""}}}, "Table 6": {"Status": "Complete", "Action": "Processed via pandas", "Inspection": {"Notes": {"Skip cause table not important": "", "Message on table quality": "Other candidate source images."}}}}}}, "Tables status": "Complete", "Inspection status": "Complete"}
